## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and current population P. This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population size through various density-dependent and density-independent mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent Malthusian growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth model)
- Theta-logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (anabolic-catabolic balance model)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth with time-dependent rate)
- Power-law growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric scaling of growth rate with population)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) + c2 * P (competition-limited growth)
- Blumberg growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 + c2 * P)**c3 (generalized flexible growth model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P â†’ density-independent (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c*P
- Quadratic term in P (PÂ² with negative coefficient) â†’ logistic-type density-dependent self-limitation
- Product P*log(P) â†’ Gompertz-type growth with logarithmic approach to carrying capacity
- Cubic or higher polynomial in P â†’ strong Allee effects or multiple equilibria in population dynamics
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 â†’ sublinear (allometric) growth, common in metabolic scaling theories
- Ratio P/(1+c*P) â†’ contest competition or resource limitation creating saturating per-capita growth
- Product of two linear factors in P â†’ bistability with Allee threshold and carrying capacity
- Time t appearing only through exp(c*t) â†’ non-autonomous growth with exponentially changing environment
- Absence of explicit t dependence â†’ autonomous ODE, growth rate determined solely by current state P
